					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the typed instance analogous to a handwritten document, see <a href="/wiki/Manuscript" title="Manuscript">manuscript</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Programming language and superset of JavaScript</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1229112069">.mw-parser-output class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.typescriptlang.org">www<wbr>.typescriptlang<wbr>.org</a></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #eee;">Influenced by</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>, <a href="/wiki/F_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="F Sharp (programming language)">F#</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #eee;">Influenced</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><a href="/wiki/AtScript" title="AtScript">AtScript</a>, <a href="/wiki/AssemblyScript" title="AssemblyScript">AssemblyScript</a>, <a href="/wiki/ArkTS" title="ArkTS">ArkTS</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>TypeScript</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source" class="mw-redirect" title="Free and open-source">free and open-source</a> <a href="/wiki/High-level_programming_language" title="High-level programming language">high-level</a> <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming language</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> that adds <a href="/wiki/Static_typing" class="mw-redirect" title="Static typing">static typing</a> with optional type <a href="/wiki/Annotation" title="Annotation">annotations</a> to <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>. It is designed for the development of large applications and <a href="/wiki/Source-to-source_compiler" title="Source-to-source compiler">transpiles</a> to JavaScript.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Because TypeScript is a <a href="/wiki/Superset" class="mw-redirect" title="Superset">superset</a> of JavaScript, all JavaScript programs are <a href="/wiki/Syntax_(programming_languages)" title="Syntax (programming languages)">syntactically</a> valid TypeScript, but they can fail to <a href="/wiki/Type_system#Type_checking" title="Type system">type-check</a> for <a href="/wiki/Type_safety" title="Type safety">safety</a> reasons.
</p><p>TypeScript may be used to develop JavaScript applications for both <a href="/wiki/Client-side" class="mw-redirect" title="Client-side">client-side</a> and <a href="/wiki/Server-side" class="mw-redirect" title="Server-side">server-side</a> execution (as with <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deno_(software)" title="Deno (software)">Deno</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bun_(software)" title="Bun (software)">Bun</a>). Multiple options are available for transpilation. The default TypeScript Compiler can be used,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/Babel_(transcompiler)" title="Babel (transcompiler)">Babel</a> compiler can be invoked to convert TypeScript to JavaScript.
</p><p>TypeScript supports definition files that can contain type information of existing JavaScript <a href="/wiki/Library_(computing)" title="Library (computing)">libraries</a>, much like <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> <a href="/wiki/Header_files" class="mw-redirect" title="Header files">header files</a> can describe the structure of existing <a href="/wiki/Object_file" title="Object file">object files</a>. This enables other programs to use the values defined in the files as if they were statically typed TypeScript entities. There are third-party header files for popular libraries such as <a href="/wiki/JQuery" title="JQuery">jQuery</a>, <a href="/wiki/MongoDB" title="MongoDB">MongoDB</a>, and <a href="/wiki/D3.js" title="D3.js">D3.js</a>. TypeScript headers for the <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a> library modules are also available, allowing development of Node.js programs within TypeScript.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>The TypeScript compiler is <a href="/wiki/Self-hosting_(compilers)" title="Self-hosting (compilers)">itself written in TypeScript</a> and <a href="/wiki/Source-to-source_compiler" title="Source-to-source compiler">compiled</a> to JavaScript. It is licensed under the <a href="/wiki/Apache_License_2.0" class="mw-redirect" title="Apache License 2.0">Apache License 2.0</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anders_Hejlsberg" title="Anders Hejlsberg">Anders Hejlsberg</a>, lead architect of <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a> and creator of <a href="/wiki/Delphi_(programming_language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Delphi (programming language)">Delphi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turbo_Pascal" title="Turbo Pascal">Turbo Pascal</a>, has worked on the development of TypeScript.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc">
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>TypeScript was released to the public in October 2012, with version 0.8, after two years of internal development at Microsoft.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Soon after the initial public release, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Icaza" title="Miguel de Icaza">Miguel de Icaza</a> praised the language itself, but criticized the lack of mature IDE support apart from <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Visual_Studio" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft Visual Studio">Microsoft Visual Studio</a>, which was not available on <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> and <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">OS X</a> at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> As of April 2021 there is support in other IDEs and text editors, including <a href="/wiki/Emacs" title="Emacs">Emacs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vim_(text_editor)" title="Vim (text editor)">Vim</a>, <a href="/wiki/JetBrains#WebStorm" title="JetBrains">WebStorm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atom_(text_editor)" title="Atom (text editor)">Atom</a><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and Microsoft's own <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio_Code" title="Visual Studio Code">Visual Studio Code</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> TypeScript 0.9, released in 2013, added support for <a href="/wiki/Generic_programming" title="Generic programming">generics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>TypeScript 1.0 was released at Microsoft's <a href="/wiki/Build_(developer_conference)" class="mw-redirect" title="Build (developer conference)">Build</a> developer conference in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual Studio 2013">Visual Studio 2013</a> Update 2 provides built-in support for TypeScript.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Further improvement were made in July 2014, when the development team announced a new TypeScript compiler, asserted to have a five-fold performance increase. Simultaneously, the source code, which was initially hosted on <a href="/wiki/CodePlex" title="CodePlex">CodePlex</a>, was moved to <a href="/wiki/GitHub" title="GitHub">GitHub</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 September 2016, TypeScript 2.0 was released, introducing several features, including the ability for programmers to optionally enforce <a href="/wiki/Null_safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Null safety">null safety</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> to mitigate what's sometimes referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Null_pointer#History" title="Null pointer">billion-dollar mistake</a>.
</p><p>TypeScript 3.0 was released on 30 July 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> bringing many language additions like tuples in rest parameters and spread expressions, rest parameters with tuple types, generic rest parameters and so on.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>TypeScript 4.0 was released on 20 August 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-26">[26]</a></sup> While 4.0 did not introduce any breaking changes, it added language features such as Custom JSX Factories and Variadic Tuple Types.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>TypeScript 5.0 was released on 16 March 2023 and included support for decorators.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Design"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>TypeScript originated from the shortcomings of JavaScript for the development of large-scale applications both at Microsoft and among their external customers.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Challenges with dealing with complex JavaScript code led to demand for custom tooling to ease developing of components in the language.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>TypeScript developers sought a solution that would not break compatibility with the standard and its cross-platform support. Knowing that the current ECMAScript standard proposal promised future support for <a href="/wiki/Class-based_programming" title="Class-based programming">class-based programming</a>, TypeScript was based on that proposal. That led to a JavaScript compiler with a set of syntactical language extensions, a superset based on the proposal, that transforms the extensions into regular JavaScript. In this sense, the class feature of TypeScript was a preview of what to expect from ECMAScript 2015. A unique aspect not in the proposal, but added to TypeScript, is optional <a href="/wiki/Static_typing" class="mw-redirect" title="Static typing">static typing</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Gradual_typing" title="Gradual typing">gradual typing</a>) that enables static language analysis to facilitate tooling and IDE support.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ECMAScript_2015_support">ECMAScript 2015 support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: ECMAScript 2015 support"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript#6th_Edition_-_ECMAScript_2015" title="ECMAScript">ECMAScript &nbsp;6th Edition - ECMAScript 2015</a></div>
<p>TypeScript adds support for features such as classes, modules, and an arrow function syntax as defined in the ECMAScript 2015 standard.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>TypeScript is a language extension that adds features to <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript" title="ECMAScript">ECMAScript</a> 6. Additional features include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Type_signature" title="Type signature">Type annotations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compile-time" class="mw-redirect" title="Compile-time">compile-time</a> <a href="/wiki/Type_checking" class="mw-redirect" title="Type checking">type checking</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Type_inference" title="Type inference">Type inference</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Type_erasure" title="Type erasure">Type erasure</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Interface_(object-oriented_programming)" title="Interface (object-oriented programming)">Interfaces</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Enumerated_type" title="Enumerated type">Enumerated types</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Generic_programming" title="Generic programming">Generics</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Namespace" title="Namespace">Namespaces</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tuple" title="Tuple">Tuples</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Async/await" title="Async/await">Async/await</a></li>
<li>Explicit Resource Management<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The following features are backported from ECMAScript 2015:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)" title="Class (computer programming)">Classes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Modular_programming" title="Modular programming">Modules</a><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>Abbreviated "arrow" syntax for <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_function" title="Anonymous function">anonymous functions</a></li>
<li>Optional parameters and <a href="/wiki/Default_parameter" class="mw-redirect" title="Default parameter">default parameters</a></li></ul>
<p>Syntactically, TypeScript is very similar to <a href="/wiki/JScript_.NET" title="JScript .NET">JScript .NET</a>, another Microsoft implementation of the ECMA-262 language standard that added support for static typing and classical object-oriented language features such as classes, inheritance, interfaces, and namespaces.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Compatibility_with_JavaScript">Compatibility with JavaScript</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Compatibility with JavaScript"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a></div>
<p>TypeScript is a strict superset of <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript" title="ECMAScript">ECMAScript</a> 2015, which is itself a superset of ECMAScript 5, commonly referred to as JavaScript.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> As such, a JavaScript program is also a valid TypeScript program and a TypeScript program can seamlessly consume JavaScript. By default the compiler targets ECMAScript 5, the current prevailing standard, but is also able to generate constructs used in ECMAScript 3 or 2015.
</p><p>With TypeScript, it is possible to use existing JavaScript code, incorporate popular JavaScript libraries, and call TypeScript-generated code from other JavaScript.<sup id="cite_ref-typescript-home-page_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-typescript-home-page-33">[33]</a></sup> Type declarations for these libraries are provided with the source code.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Type_annotations">Type annotations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Type annotations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>TypeScript provides <a href="/wiki/Static_typing" class="mw-redirect" title="Static typing">static typing</a> through type annotations to enable <a href="/wiki/Type_checking" class="mw-redirect" title="Type checking">type checking</a> at <a href="/wiki/Compile_time" title="Compile time">compile time</a>. This is optional and can be ignored to use the regular <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_typing" class="mw-redirect" title="Dynamic typing">dynamic typing</a> of JavaScript.
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-typescript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kd">function</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">add</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">left</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">right</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">	</span><span class="k">return</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">left</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">+</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">right</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</pre></div>
<p>Primitive types are annotated using the types <code>number</code>, <code>boolean</code>, and <code>string</code>. These types are distinct from their class counterparts (<code>Number</code>, <code>Boolean</code>, etc), which cannot have operations performed from values directly. For instance, a <code>Number</code> and a <code>number</code> cannot be added. There is additionally <code>undefined</code> and <code>null</code> types for their respective values.
</p><p>All other types are annotated using their class name rather than primitives, such as <code>Error</code>. Arrays can be written in two different ways which are both syntactically the same: the generic-based syntax <code>Array&lt;T&gt;</code> and a shorthand with <code>T[]</code>.
</p><p>Additional built-in data types are tuples, unions, <code>never</code> and <code>any</code>:
</p>
<ul><li>An array with predefined data types at each index is a tuple, represented as <code>[type1, type2, ..., typeN]</code>.</li>
<li>A variable that can hold more than one type of data is a union, represented using the logical OR <code>|</code> symbol (<code>string | number</code>).</li>
<li>The <code>never</code> type is used when a given type should be impossible to create, which is useful for filtering mapped types.</li>
<li>A value of type <code>any</code> supports the same operations as a value in JavaScript and minimal static type checking is performed,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> which makes it suitable for weakly or dynamically-typed structures, although this is generally discouraged practice.<sup id="cite_ref-TypeScript_Language_Specification_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TypeScript_Language_Specification-35">[35]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Type annotations can be exported to a separate <i>declarations file</i> to make type information available for TypeScript scripts using types already compiled into JavaScript. Annotations can be declared for an existing JavaScript library, as has been done for <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a> and <a href="/wiki/JQuery" title="JQuery">jQuery</a>.
</p><p>The TypeScript compiler makes use of <a href="/wiki/Type_inference" title="Type inference">type inference</a> to infer types when types are not given. For example, the <code>add</code> method in the code above would be inferred as returning a <code>number</code> even if no return type annotation had been provided. This is based on the static types of <code>left</code> and <code>right</code> being <code>numbers</code>, and the compiler's knowledge that the result of adding two <code>number</code>s is always a <code>number</code>. However, explicitly declaring the return type allows the compiler to verify correctness.
</p><p>If no type can be inferred because of lack of declarations (such as in a JavaScript module without types), then it defaults to the dynamic <code>any</code> type. Additional module types can be provided using a .d.ts declaration file using the <code>declare module "moduleName"</code> syntax.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Declaration_files">Declaration files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Declaration files"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>When a TypeScript script gets compiled there is an option to generate a <i>declaration file</i> (with the extension <code>.d.ts</code>) that functions as an <a href="/wiki/Interface_(computing)" title="Interface (computing)">interface</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Component-oriented_programming" class="mw-redirect" title="Component-oriented programming">components</a> in the compiled JavaScript. In the process the compiler strips away all function and method bodies and preserves only the signatures of the types that are exported. The resulting declaration file can then be used to describe the exported virtual TypeScript types of a JavaScript library or module when a third-party developer consumes it from TypeScript.
</p><p>The concept of declaration files is analogous to the concept of <a href="/wiki/Header_file" class="mw-redirect" title="Header file">header files</a> found in <a href="/wiki/C/C%2B%2B" class="mw-redirect" title="C/C++">C/C++</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-typescript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kr">declare</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">namespace</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Arithmetics</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nx">add</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">left</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">right</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nx">subtract</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">left</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">right</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nx">multiply</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">left</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">right</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nx">divide</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">left</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">right</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</pre></div>
<p>Type declaration files can be written by hand for existing JavaScript libraries, as has been done for jQuery and Node.js.
</p><p>Large collections of declaration files for popular JavaScript libraries are hosted on GitHub in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://github.com/DefinitelyTyped/DefinitelyTyped">DefinitelyTyped</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generics">Generics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Generics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Generic_programming" title="Generic programming">Generic programming</a></div>
<p>TypeScript supports <a href="/wiki/Generic_programming" title="Generic programming">generic programming</a> using a syntax similar to <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The following is an example of the <a href="/wiki/Identity_function" title="Identity function">identity function</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-typescript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kd">function</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">id</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nx">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">x</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">T</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">T</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">return</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">x</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</pre></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classes">Classes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Classes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>TypeScript uses the same annotation style for class methods and fields as for functions and variables respectively. Compared with vanilla JavaScript classes, a TypeScript class can also implement an interface through the <code>implements</code> keyword, use generic parameters similarly to <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, and specify public and private fields.
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-typescript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kd">class</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Person</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">private</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">name</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">string</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">private</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">age</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">private</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">salary</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">;</span>

<span class="w">    </span><span class="kr">constructor</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">name</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">string</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">age</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">salary</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="k">this</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">name</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">name</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="k">this</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">age</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">age</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="k">this</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">salary</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">salary</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span>

<span class="w">    </span><span class="nx">toString</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">string</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="k">return</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sb">`</span><span class="si">${</span><span class="k">this</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">name</span><span class="si">}</span><span class="sb"> (</span><span class="si">${</span><span class="k">this</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">age</span><span class="si">}</span><span class="sb">) (</span><span class="si">${</span><span class="k">this</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">salary</span><span class="si">}</span><span class="sb">)`</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</pre></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_types">Union types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Union types"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Union_type#TypeScript" title="Union type">Union type  TypeScript</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Union_type&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>Union types are supported in TypeScript.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The values are implicitly "tagged" with a type by the language, and may be retrieved using a <code>typeof</code> call for primitive values and an <code>instanceof</code> comparison for complex data types. Types with overlapping usage (e.g. a slice method exists on both strings and arrays, the plus operator works on both strings and numbers) don't need additional narrowing to use these features.
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-typescript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kd">function</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">successor</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">n</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">bigint</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">bigint</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// types that support the same operations don't need narrowing</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">return</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">++</span><span class="nx">n</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="p">}</span>

<span class="kd">function</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">dependsOnParameter</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">v</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">string</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Array</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">string</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">number</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// distinct types need narrowing</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="k">if</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="ow">instanceof</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Array</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="c1">// do something</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">else</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">if</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">(</span><span class="ow">typeof</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">v</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">===</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"string"</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="c1">// do something else</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">else</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="c1">// has to be a number</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</pre></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enumerated_types">Enumerated types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Enumerated types"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Enumerated_type#TypeScript" title="Enumerated type">Enumerated type  TypeScript</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Enumerated_type&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>TypeScript adds an 'enum' data type to JavaScript.
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-javascript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kr">enum</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="nx">Clubs</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Diamonds</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Hearts</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Spades</span><span class="p">};</span>
<span class="kd">var</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">c</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">Diamonds</span><span class="p">;</span>
</pre></div>
<p>By default, enums number members starting at 0; this can be overridden by setting the value of the first:
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-javascript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kr">enum</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="nx">Clubs</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Diamonds</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Hearts</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Spades</span><span class="p">};</span>
<span class="kd">var</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">c</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">Diamonds</span><span class="p">;</span>
</pre></div>
<p>All the values can be set:
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-javascript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kr">enum</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="nx">Clubs</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Diamonds</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Hearts</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Spades</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">8</span><span class="p">};</span>
<span class="kd">var</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">c</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">Diamonds</span><span class="p">;</span>
</pre></div>
<p>TypeScript supports mapping the numeric value to its name. For example, this finds the name of the value 2:
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-javascript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="kr">enum</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="nx">Clubs</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Diamonds</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Hearts</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Spades</span><span class="p">};</span>
<span class="kd">var</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">suitName</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">string</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nx">Cardsuit</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mf">2</span><span class="p">];</span>

<span class="nx">alert</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">suitName</span><span class="p">);</span>
</pre></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modules_and_namespaces">Modules and namespaces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Modules and namespaces"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>TypeScript distinguishes between modules and namespaces. Both features in TypeScript support encapsulation of classes, interfaces, functions and variables into containers. Namespaces (formerly internal modules) utilize JavaScript <a href="/wiki/Immediately-invoked_function_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Immediately-invoked function expression">immediately-invoked function expressions</a> to encapsulate code, whereas modules (formerly external modules) leverage JavaScript library patterns to do so (<a href="/wiki/Asynchronous_module_definition" title="Asynchronous module definition">AMD</a> or <a href="/wiki/CommonJS" title="CommonJS">CommonJS</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_tools">Development tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Development tools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Compiler">Compiler</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Compiler"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The TypeScript compiler, named <code>tsc</code>, is <a href="/wiki/Self-hosting_(compilers)" title="Self-hosting (compilers)">written in TypeScript</a>. As a result, it can be compiled into regular JavaScript and can then be executed in any JavaScript engine (e.g. a browser). The compiler package comes bundled with a script host that can execute the compiler. It is also available as a <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a> package that uses Node.js as a host.
</p><p>The compiler can "target" a particular edition of ECMAScript (such as <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript_version_history" title="ECMAScript version history">ES5</a> for legacy browser compatibility), but by default compiles to the latest version.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IDE_and_editor_support">IDE and editor support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: IDE and editor support"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> provides a <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plug-in</a> for <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio" title="Visual Studio">Visual Studio 2012</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_WebMatrix" title="Microsoft WebMatrix">WebMatrix</a>, full integrated support in <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio" title="Visual Studio">Visual Studio 2013</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio" title="Visual Studio">Visual Studio 2015</a>, and basic text editor support for <a href="/wiki/Emacs" title="Emacs">Emacs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vim_(text_editor)" title="Vim (text editor)">Vim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-blogs.msdn.com_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.msdn.com-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio_Code" title="Visual Studio Code">Visual Studio Code</a> supports TypeScript in addition to several other languages, and offers features like debugging and intelligent <a href="/wiki/Code_completion" title="Code completion">code completion</a>.</li>
<li>alm.tools is an open source cloud IDE for TypeScript built using TypeScript, ReactJS and TypeStyle.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JetBrains" title="JetBrains">JetBrains</a> supports TypeScript with code completion, refactoring and debugging in its IDEs built on IntelliJ platform, such as <a href="/wiki/PhpStorm" class="mw-redirect" title="PhpStorm">PhpStorm</a> 6, <a href="/wiki/WebStorm" class="mw-redirect" title="WebStorm">WebStorm</a> 6, and <a href="/wiki/IntelliJ_IDEA" title="IntelliJ IDEA">IntelliJ IDEA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> as well as their Visual Studio Add-in and extension, ReSharper 8.1.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atom_(text_editor)" title="Atom (text editor)">Atom</a> has a TypeScript plugin with support for code completion, navigation, formatting, and fast compilation.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li>The online <a href="/wiki/Cloud9_IDE" title="Cloud9 IDE">Cloud9 IDE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Codenvy" class="mw-redirect" title="Codenvy">Codenvy</a> support TypeScript.</li>
<li>A plugin is available for the <a href="/wiki/NetBeans" title="NetBeans">NetBeans IDE</a>.</li>
<li>A plugin is available for the <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_(software)" title="Eclipse (software)">Eclipse IDE</a> (version Kepler)</li>
<li>TypEcs is available for the <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_(software)" title="Eclipse (software)">Eclipse IDE</a>.</li>
<li>The Cross Platform Cloud IDE <a href="/wiki/Codeanywhere" title="Codeanywhere">Codeanywhere</a> supports TypeScript.</li>
<li>Webclipse An Eclipse plugin designed to develop TypeScript and <a href="/wiki/Angular_(application_platform)" class="mw-redirect" title="Angular (application platform)">Angular 2</a>.</li>
<li>Angular IDE A standalone IDE available via npm to develop TypeScript and Angular 2 applications, with integrated terminal support.</li>
<li>Tide&nbsp;  TypeScript Interactive Development Environment for <a href="/wiki/Emacs" title="Emacs">Emacs</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Integration_with_build_automation_tools">Integration with build automation tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Integration with build automation tools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Build_automation" title="Build automation">Build automation</a></div>
<p>Using <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plug-ins</a>, TypeScript can be integrated with <a href="/wiki/Build_automation" title="Build automation">build automation</a> tools, including Grunt (grunt-ts<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Apache_Maven" title="Apache Maven">Apache Maven</a> (TypeScript Maven Plugin<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>), Gulp (gulp-typescript<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Gradle" title="Gradle">Gradle</a> (TypeScript Gradle Plugin<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Linting_tools">Linting tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Linting tools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>TSLint<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> scans TypeScript code for conformance to a set of standards and guidelines. <a href="/wiki/ESLint" title="ESLint">ESLint</a>, a standard JavaScript linter, also provided some support for TypeScript via community plugins. However, ESLint's inability to leverage TypeScript's language services precluded certain forms of semantic linting and program-wide analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In early 2019, the TSLint team announced the linter's deprecation in favor of <code>typescript-eslint</code>, a joint effort of the TSLint, ESLint and TypeScript teams to consolidate linting under the ESLint umbrella for improved performance, community unity and developer accessibility.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CodeDOM_Provider">CodeDOM Provider</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TypeScript&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: CodeDOM Provider"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>CodeDOM<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> provides types that represent common types of source code elements, which will be transformed to data types, classes and statements etc. of a programming language through a CodeDOMProvider.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Programmers use CodeDOM and a CodeDOM provider to construct a code generator that generates codes for an application domain.
TypeScript CodeDOM Provider<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> generates TypeScript codes according to a CodeDOM.
</p>
